On the dissent's view, it must have been wrong for <em>West Virginia Bd. of Ed. </em>v. <em>Barnette</em>, 319 U.&nbsp;S. 624, to overrule <em>Minersville School Dist. </em>v<em>. Gobitis</em>, 310 U.&nbsp;S. 586, a bare three years after it was handed down.  In both cases, children who were Jehovah's Witnesses refused on religious grounds to salute the flag or recite the pledge of allegiance.  The <em>Barnette </em>Court did not claim that its reexamination of the issue was prompted by any intervening legal or factual developments, so if the Court had followed the dissent's new version of <em>stare decisis, </em>it would have been compelled to adhere to <em>Gobitis </em>and countenance continued First Amendment violations for some unspecified period.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Precedents should be respected, but sometimes the Court errs, and occasionally the Court issues an important decision that is egregiously wrong.  When that happens, <em>stare decisis</em> is not a straitjacket.  And indeed, the dissent eventually admits that a decision <em>could </em>"be overruled just because it is terribly wrong," though the dissent does not explain when that would be so.  <em>Post</em>, at 45.</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">2</p>
</h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Even if the dissent were correct in arguing that an egregiously wrong decision should (almost) never be overruled unless its mistake is later highlighted by "major legal or factual changes," reexamination of <em>Roe</em> and <em>Casey</em> would be amply justified.  We have already mentioned a number of post-<em>Casey</em> developments, see <em>supra</em>,<em> </em>at 33-34, 59-63, but the most profound change may be the failure of the <em>Casey </em>plurality's call for "the contending sides" in the controversy about abortion "to end their national division," 505 U.&nbsp;S., at 867.  That has not happened, and there is no reason to think that another decision sticking with <em>Roe</em> would achieve what <em>Casey</em> could not.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The dissent, however, is undeterred.  It contends that the "very controversy surrounding <em>Roe </em>and <em>Casey</em>" is an important <em>stare decisis </em>consideration that requires upholding those precedents.  See <em>post, </em>at 55-57.  The dissent characterizes <em>Casey </em>as a "precedent about precedent" that is permanently shielded from further evaluation under traditional <em>stare decisis </em>principles.  See <em>post,</em> at 57.  But as we have explained, <em>Casey</em> broke new ground when it treated the national controversy provoked by <em>Roe</em> as a ground for refusing to reconsider that decision, and no subsequent case has relied on that factor.  Our decision today simply applies longstanding <em>stare decisis </em>factors instead of applying a version of the doctrine that seems to apply only in abortion cases.</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">3</p>
</h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Finally, the dissent suggests that our decision calls into question <em>Griswold</em>, <em>Eisenstadt</em>, <em>Lawrence</em>, and <em>Obergefell</em>.  <em>Post</em>, at 4-5, 26-27, n. 8.  But we have stated unequivocally that "[n]othing in this opinion should be understood to cast doubt on precedents that do not concern abortion."  <em>Supra</em>, at 66.  We have also explained why that is so: rights regarding contraception and same-sex relationships are inherently different from the right to abortion because the latter (as we have stressed) uniquely involves what <em>Roe</em> and <em>Casey</em> termed "potential life."  <em>Roe</em>, 410 U.&nbsp;S., at 150 (emphasis deleted); <em>Casey</em>, 505 U.&nbsp;S., at 852.  Therefore, a right to abortion cannot be justified by a purported analogy to the rights recognized in those other cases or by "appeals to a broader right to autonomy."  <em>Supra</em>, at 32.  It is hard to see how we could be clearer.  Moreover, even putting aside that these cases are distinguishable, there is a further point that the dissent ignores: Each precedent is subject to its own <em>stare decisis</em> analysis, and the factors that our doctrine instructs us to consider like reliance and workability are different for these cases than for our abortion jurisprudence.</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">B</p>
</h2><h3><p align="CENTER">1</p>
</h3><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We now turn to the concurrence in the judgment, which reproves us for deciding whether <em>Roe </em>and <em>Casey</em> should be retained or overruled.  That opinion (which for convenience we will call simply "the concurrence") recommends a "more measured course," which it defends based on what it claims is "a straightforward <em>stare decisis</em> analysis."  <em>Post</em>, at 1 (opinion of <span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Roberts</small></span>, C.&nbsp;J.).  The concurrence would "leave for another day whether to reject any right to an abortion at all," <em>post</em>, at 7, and would hold only that if the Constitution protects any such right, the right ends once women have had "a reasonable opportunity" to obtain an abortion, <em>post</em>, at 1.  The concurrence does not specify what period of time is sufficient to provide such an opportunity, but it would hold that 15 weeks, the period allowed under Mississippi's law, is enough--at least "absent rare circumstances."  <em>Post</em>, at 2, 10.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;There are serious problems with this approach, and it is revealing that nothing like it was recommended by either party.  As we have recounted, both parties and the Solicitor General have urged us either to reaffirm or overrule <em>Roe</em> and <em>Casey</em>.  See <em>supra</em>, at 4-5.  And when the specific approach advanced by the concurrence was broached at oral argument, both respondents and the Solicitor General emphatically rejected it.  Respondents' counsel termed it "completely unworkable" and "less principled and less workable than viability."  Tr. of Oral Arg. 54.  The Solicitor General argued that abandoning the viability line would leave courts and others with "no continued guidance."  <em>Id</em>., at 101.  What is more, the concurrence has not identified any of the more than 130 <em>amicus</em> briefs filed in this case that advocated its approach.  The concurrence would do exactly what it criticizes <em>Roe</em> for doing: pulling "out of thin air" a test that "[n]o party or <em>amicus</em> asked the Court to adopt."  <em>Post</em>, at 3.</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">2</p>
</h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The concurrence's most fundamental defect is its failure to offer any principled basis for its approach.  The concurrence would "discar[d]" "the rule from <em>Roe</em> and <em>Casey</em> that a woman's right to terminate her pregnancy extends up to the point that the fetus is regarded as 'viable' outside the womb."  <em>Post</em>, at 2.  But this rule was a critical component of the holdings in <em>Roe</em> and <em>Casey</em>, and <em>stare decisis</em> is "a doctrine of preservation, not transformation," <em>Citizens United </em>v.<em> Federal Election Comm'n</em>, 558 U.&nbsp;S. 310, 384 (2010) (<span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Roberts</small></span>, C.&nbsp;J., concurring).  Therefore, a new rule that discards the viability rule cannot be defended on <em>stare decisis</em> grounds.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The concurrence concedes that its approach would "not be available" if "the rationale of <em>Roe</em> and <em>Casey</em> were inextricably entangled with and dependent upon the viability standard."  <em>Post</em>, at 7.  But the concurrence asserts that the viability line is separable from the constitutional right they recognized, and can therefore be "discarded" without disturbing any past precedent.  <em>Post</em>, at 7-8.  That is simply incorrect.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<em>Ro</em>e's trimester rule was expressly tied to viability, see 410 U.&nbsp;S., at 163-164, and viability played a critical role in later abortion decisions.  For example, in <em>Planned Parenthood of Central Mo</em>. v.<em> Danforth</em>, 428 U.&nbsp;S. 52, the Court reiterated <em>Roe</em>'s rule that a "State may regulate an abortion to protect the life of the fetus and even may proscribe abortion" at "the stage <em>subsequent to viability</em>."  428 U.&nbsp;S., at 61 (emphasis added).  The Court then rejected a challenge to Missouri's definition of viability, holding that the State's definition was consistent with <em>Roe</em>'s.  428 U.&nbsp;S., at 63-64.  If viability was not an essential part of the rule adopted in <em>Roe</em>, the Court would have had no need to make that comparison.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The holding in <em>Colautti </em>v.<em> Franklin</em>, 439 U.&nbsp;S. 379, is even more instructive.  In that case, the Court noted that prior cases had "stressed viability" and reiterated that "[v]iability is the critical point" under <em>Roe.  </em>439 U.&nbsp;S.,<em> </em>at 388-389.  It then struck down Pennsylvania's definition of viability, <em>id.</em>, at 389-394, and it is hard to see how the Court could have done that if <em>Roe</em>'s discussion of viability was not part of its holding.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When the Court reconsidered <em>Roe </em>in <em>Casey</em>, it left no doubt about the importance of the viability rule.  It described the rule as <em>Roe</em>'s "central holding," 505 U.&nbsp;S., at 860, and repeatedly stated that the right it reaffirmed was "the right of the woman to choose to have an abortion <em>before viability</em>."  <em>Id</em>., at 846 (emphasis added).  See <em>id</em>., at 871 ("The woman's right to terminate her pregnancy <em>before viability</em> is the most central principle of <em>Roe </em>v.<em> Wade</em>.  It is a rule of law and a component of liberty we cannot renounce" (emphasis added)); <em>id</em>., at 872 (A "woman has a right to choose to terminate or continue her pregnancy <em>before viability</em>" (emphasis added)); <em>id</em>., at 879 ("[A] State may not prohibit any woman from making the ultimate decision to terminate her pregnancy <em>before viability</em>" (emphasis added)).</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our subsequent cases have continued to recognize the centrality of the viability rule.  See <em>Whole Women's Health</em>, 579 U.&nbsp;S., at 589-590 ("[A] provision of law is constitutionally invalid, if the 'purpose or effect' of the provision 'is to place a substantial obstacle in the path of a woman seeking an abortion <em>before the fetus attains viability</em>'&nbsp;" (emphasis deleted and added)); <em>id.</em>, at 627 ("[W]e now use <em>'viability'</em> as the relevant point at which a State may begin limiting women's access to abortion for reasons unrelated to maternal health" (emphasis added)).</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Not only is the new rule proposed by the concurrence inconsistent with <em>Casey'</em>s unambiguous "language," <em>post</em>, at 8, it is also contrary to the judgment in that case and later abortion cases.  In <em>Casey</em>, the Court held that Pennsylvania's spousal-notification provision was facially unconstitutional, not just that it was unconstitutional as applied to abortions sought prior to the time when a woman has had a reasonable opportunity to choose.  See 505 U.&nbsp;S., at 887-898.  The same is true of <em>Whole Women's Health</em>, which held that certain rules that required physicians performing abortions to have admitting privileges at a nearby hospital were facially unconstitutional because they placed "a substantial obstacle in the path of women seeking <em>a previability abortion</em>."  579 U.&nbsp;S., at 591 (emphasis added).</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For all these reasons, <em>stare decisis</em> cannot justify the new "reasonable opportunity" rule propounded by the concurrence.  If that rule is to become the law of the land, it must stand on its own, but the concurrence makes no attempt to show that this rule represents a correct interpretation of the Constitution.  The concurrence does not claim that the right to a reasonable opportunity to obtain an abortion is "&nbsp;'deeply rooted in this Nation's history and tradition'&nbsp;" and "&nbsp;'implicit in the concept of ordered liberty.'&nbsp;"  <em>Glucksberg</em>, 521 U.&nbsp;S., at 720-721.  Nor does it propound any other theory that could show that the Constitution supports its new rule.  And if the Constitution protects a woman's right to obtain an abortion, the opinion does not explain why that right should end after the point at which all "reasonable" women will have decided whether to seek an abortion.  While the concurrence is moved by a desire for judicial minimalism, "we cannot embrace a narrow ground of decision simply because it is narrow; it must also be right."  <em>Citizens United</em>, 558 U.&nbsp;S., at 375 (<span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Roberts</small></span>, C.&nbsp;J., concurring).  For the reasons that we have explained, the concurrence's approach is not.</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">3</p>
</h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The concurrence would "leave for another day whether to reject any right to an abortion at all," <em>post</em>, at 7, but "another day" would not be long in coming.  Some States have set deadlines for obtaining an abortion that are shorter than Mississippi's.  See, <em>e.g.</em>, <em>Memphis Center for Reproductive Health </em>v. <em>Slatery</em>, 14 F. 4th, at 414 (considering law with bans "at cascading intervals of two to three weeks" beginning at six weeks), reh'g en banc granted, 14 F. 4th 550 (CA6 2021).  If we held only that Mississippi's 15-week rule is constitutional, we would soon be called upon to pass on the constitutionality of a panoply of laws with shorter deadlines or no deadline at all.  The "measured course" charted by the concurrence would be fraught with turmoil until the Court answered the question that the concurrence seeks to defer.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Even if the Court ultimately adopted the new rule suggested by the concurrence, we would be faced with the difficult problem of spelling out what it means.  For example, if the period required to give women a "reasonable" opportunity to obtain an abortion were pegged, as the concurrence seems to suggest, at the point when a certain percentage of women make that choice, see <em>post</em>, at 1-2, 9-10, we would have to identify the relevant percentage.  It would also be necessary to explain what the concurrence means when it refers to "rare circumstances" that might justify an exception.  <em>Post</em>, at 10.  And if this new right aims to give women a reasonable opportunity to get an abortion, it would be necessary to decide whether factors other than promptness in deciding might have a bearing on whether such an opportunity was available.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In sum, the concurrence's quest for a middle way would only put off the day when we would be forced to confront the question we now decide.  The turmoil wrought by <em>Roe</em> and <em>Casey</em> would be prolonged.  It is far better--for this Court and the country--to face up to the real issue without further delay.</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">VI</p>
</h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We must now decide what standard will govern if state abortion regulations undergo constitutional challenge and whether the law before us satisfies the appropriate standard.</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">A</p>
</h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under our precedents, rational-basis review is the appropriate standard for such challenges.  As we have explained, procuring an abortion is not a fundamental constitutional right because such a right has no basis in the Constitution's text or in our Nation's history.  See <em>supra,</em> at 8-39.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;It follows that the States may regulate abortion for legitimate reasons, and when such regulations are challenged under the Constitution, courts cannot "substitute their social and economic beliefs for the judgment of legislative bodies."  <em>Ferguson</em>, 372 U.&nbsp;S., at 729-730; see also <em>Dandridge </em>v. <em>Williams</em>, 397 U.&nbsp;S. 471, 484-486 (1970); <em>United States </em>v. <em>Carolene Products Co.</em>, 304 U.&nbsp;S. 144, 152 (1938).  That respect for a legislature's judgment applies even when the laws at issue concern matters of great social significance and moral substance.  See, <em>e.g.,</em> <em>Board of Trustees of Univ. of Ala.</em> v. <em>Garrett</em>, 531 U.&nbsp;S. 356, 365-368 (2001) ("treatment of the disabled"); <em>Glucksberg</em>, 521 U.&nbsp;S., at 728 ("assisted suicide"); <em>San Antonio Independent School Dist.</em> v. <em>Rodriguez</em>, 411 U.&nbsp;S. 1, 32-35, 55 (1973) ("financing public education").</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A law regulating abortion, like other health and welfare laws, is entitled to a "strong presumption of validity."  <em>Heller </em>v.<em> Doe</em>, 509 U.&nbsp;S. 312, 319 (1993).  It must be sustained if there is a rational basis on which the legislature could have thought that it would serve legitimate state interests.  <em>Id.,</em> at 320; <em>FCC </em>v. <em>Beach Communications</em>, <em>Inc</em>., 508 U.&nbsp;S. 307, 313 (1993); <em>New Orleans </em>v.<em> Dukes</em>, 427 U.&nbsp;S. 297, 303 (1976) (<em>per&nbsp;curiam</em>); <em>Williamson</em> v. <em>Lee Optical of Okla., Inc.</em>, 348 U.&nbsp;S. 483, 491 (1955).  These legitimate interests include respect for and preservation of prenatal life at all stages of development, <em>Gonzales</em>, 550 U.&nbsp;S., at 157-158; the protection of maternal health and safety; the elimination of particularly gruesome or barbaric medical procedures; the preservation of the integrity of the medical profession; the mitigation of fetal pain; and the prevention of discrimination on the basis of race, sex, or disability.  See <em>id.</em>, at 156-157; <em>Roe</em>, 410 U.&nbsp;S., at 150; cf. <em>Glucksberg</em>, 521 U.&nbsp;S., at 728-731 (identifying similar interests).</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">B</p>
</h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;These legitimate interests justify Mississippi's Gestational Age Act.  Except "in a medical emergency or in the case of a severe fetal abnormality," the statute prohibits abortion "if the probable gestational age of the unborn human being has been determined to be greater than fifteen (15) weeks."  Miss. Code Ann. §41-41-191(4)(b).  The Mississippi Legislature's findings recount the stages of "human prenatal development" and assert the State's interest in "protecting the life of the unborn."  §2(b)(i).  The legislature also found that abortions performed after 15 weeks typically use the dilation and evacuation procedure, and the legislature found the use of this procedure "for nontherapeutic or elective reasons [to be] a barbaric practice, dangerous for the maternal patient, and demeaning to the medical profession."  §2(b)(i)(8); see also <em>Gonzales</em>, 550 U.&nbsp;S., at 135-143 (describing such procedures).  These legitimate interests provide a rational basis for the Gestational Age Act, and it follows that respondents' constitutional challenge must fail.</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">VII</p>
</h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We end this opinion where we began.  Abortion presents a profound moral question.  The Constitution does not prohibit the citizens of each State from regulating or prohibiting abortion.  <em>Roe</em> and <em>Casey</em> arrogated that authority.  We now overrule those decisions and return that authority to the people and their elected representatives.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The judgment of the Fifth Circuit is reversed, and the case is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.</p>
<p align="RIGHT">It is so ordered.</p>
<h2><p align="CENTER">APPENDICES</p>
</h2><h3><p align="CENTER">A</p>
</h3><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This appendix contains statutes criminalizing abortion at all stages of pregnancy in the States existing in 1868.  The statutes appear in chronological order.</p>
<p><strong>1. Missouri (1825):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 12. "That every person who shall wilfully and maliciously administer or cause to be administered to or taken by any person, any poison, or other noxious, poisonous or destructive substance or liquid, with an intention to harm him or her thereby to murder, or thereby<em> to cause or procure the miscarriage of any woman then being with child</em>, and shall thereof be duly convicted, shall suffer imprisonment not exceeding seven years, and be fined not exceeding three thousand dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 69" name="FRopinion1.69" href="#FNopinion1.69">69</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>2. Illinois (1827):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 46. "Every person who shall wilfully and maliciously administer, or cause to be administered to, or taken by any person, any poison, or other noxious or destructive substance or liquid, with an intention to cause the death of such person, <em>or to procure the miscarriage of any woman, then being with child</em>, and shall thereof be duly convicted, shall be imprisoned for a term not exceeding three years, and be fined in a sum not exceeding one thousand dollars."<sup> </sup><sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 70" name="FRopinion1.70" href="#FNopinion1.70">70</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>3. New York (1828):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 9. "Every person who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with a quick child</em>, any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such mother, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for such purpose, shall, in case the death of such child or of such mother be thereby produced, be deemed guilty of manslaughter in the second degree."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 21. "Every person who shall willfully administer <em>to any pregnant woman</em>, any medicine, drug, substance or thing whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument of other means whatever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of any such woman, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such woman, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for that purpose; shall, upon conviction, be punished by imprisonment in a county jail not more than one year, or by fine not exceeding five hundred dollars, or by both such fine and imprisonment."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 71" name="FRopinion1.71" href="#FNopinion1.71">71</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>4. Ohio (1834):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "Be it enacted by the General Assembly of State of Ohio, That any physician, or other person, who shall wilfully administer <em>to any pregnant woman</em> any medicine, drug, substance, or thing whatever, or shall use any instrument or other means whatever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of any such woman, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such woman, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for that purpose, shall, upon conviction, be punished by imprisonment in the county jail not more than one year, or by fine not exceeding five hundred dollars, or by both such fine and imprisonment."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "That any physician, or other person, who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with a quick child</em>, any medicine, drug, or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument, or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such mother, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for such purpose, shall, in case of the death of such child or mother in consequence thereof, be deemed guilty of high misdemeanor, and, upon conviction thereof, shall be imprisoned in the penitentiary not more than seven years, nor less than one year."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 72" name="FRopinion1.72" href="#FNopinion1.72">72</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>5. Indiana (1835):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 3.  "That every person who shall wilfully administer <em>to</em> <em>any pregnant woman</em>, any medicine, drug, substance or thing whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means whatever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of any such woman, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such woman, shall upon conviction be punished by imprisonment in the county jail any term of [time] not exceeding twelve months and be fined any sum not exceeding five hundred dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 73" name="FRopinion1.73" href="#FNopinion1.73">73</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>6. Maine (1840):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 13. "Every person, who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with child, whether such child be quick or not</em>, any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means whatever, with intent to destroy such child, and shall thereby destroy such child before its birth, unless the same shall have been done as necessary to preserve the life of the mother, shall be punished by imprisonment in the state prison, not more than five years, or by fine, not exceeding one thousand dollars, and imprisonment in the county jail, not more than one year."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 14. "Every person, who shall administer <em>to any woman, pregnant with child, whether such child shall be quick or not</em>, any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means whatever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of such woman, unless the same shall have been done, as necessary to preserve her life, shall be punished by imprisonment in the county jail, not more than one year, or by fine, not exceeding one thousand dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 74" name="FRopinion1.74" href="#FNopinion1.74">74</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>7. Alabama (1841):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "Every person who shall wilfully administer <em>to any pregnant woman </em>any medicines, drugs, substance or thing whatever, or shall use and employ any instrument or means whatever with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of such woman, unless the same shall be necessary to preserve her life, or shall have been advised by a respectable physician to be necessary for that purpose, shall upon conviction, be punished by fine not exceeding five hundred dollars, and by imprisonment in the county jail, not less than three, and not exceeding six months."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 75" name="FRopinion1.75" href="#FNopinion1.75">75</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>8. Massachusetts (1845):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ch. 27. "Whoever, maliciously or without lawful justification, with  intent to cause and procure the miscarriage <em>of a woman then pregnant with child</em>, shall administer to her, prescribe for her, or advise or direct her to take or swallow, any poison, drug, medicine or noxious thing, or shall cause or procure her with like intent, to take or swallow any poison, drug, medicine or noxious thing; and whoever maliciously and without lawful justification, shall use any instrument or means whatever with the like intent, and every person, with the like intent, knowingly aiding and assisting such offender or offenders, shall be deemed guilty of felony, if the woman die in consequence thereof, and shall be imprisoned not more than twenty years, nor less than five years in the State Prison; and if the woman doth not die in consequence thereof, such offender shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and shall be punished by imprisonment not exceeding seven years, nor less than one year, in the state prison or house of correction, or common jail, and by fine not exceeding two thousand dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 76" name="FRopinion1.76" href="#FNopinion1.76">76</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>9. Michigan (1846):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 33. "Every person who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with a quick child</em>, any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such mother, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for such purpose, shall, in case the death of such child or of such mother be thereby produced, be deemed guilty of manslaughter."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 34. "Every person who shall wilfully administer <em>to</em> <em>any pregnant woman</em> any medicine, drug, substance or thing whatever, or shall employ any instrument or other means whatever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of any such woman, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such woman, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for that purpose, shall, upon conviction, be punished by imprisonment in a county jail not more than one year, or by a fine not exceeding five hundred dollars, or by both such fine and imprisonment."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 77" name="FRopinion1.77" href="#FNopinion1.77">77</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>10. Vermont (1846):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "Whoever maliciously, or without lawful justification with intent to cause and procure the miscarriage <em>of a woman, then pregnant with child,</em> shall administer to her, prescribe for her, or advise or direct her to take or swallow any poison, drug, medicine or noxious thing, or shall cause or procure her, with like intent, to take or swallow any poison, drug, medicine or noxious thing, and whoever maliciously and without lawful justification, shall use any instrument or means whatever, with the like intent, and every person, with the like intent, knowingly aiding and assisting such offenders, shall be deemed guilty of felony, if the woman die in consequence thereof, and shall be imprisoned in the state prison, not more than ten years, nor less than five years; and if the woman does not die in consequence thereof, such offenders shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor; and shall be punished by imprisonment in the state prison not exceeding three years, nor less than one year, and pay a fine not exceeding two hundred dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 78" name="FRopinion1.78" href="#FNopinion1.78">78</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>11. Virginia (1848):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 9. "Any free person who shall administer <em>to any pregnant woman</em>, any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or use or employ any instrument or other means with intent thereby to destroy the child with which such woman may be pregnant, or to produce abortion or miscarriage, and shall thereby destroy such child, or produce such abortion or miscarriage, unless the same shall have been done to preserve the life of such woman, shall be punished, if the death of a quick child be thereby produced, by confinement in the penitentiary, for not less than one nor more than five years, or if the death of a child, not quick, be thereby produced, by confinement in the jail for not less than one nor more than twelve months."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 79" name="FRopinion1.79" href="#FNopinion1.79">79</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>12. New Hampshire (1849):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "That every person, who shall wilfully administer <em>to any pregnant woman</em>, any medicine, drug, substance or thing whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or means whatever with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of any such woman, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such woman, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for that purpose, shall, upon conviction, be punished by imprisonment in the county jail not more than one year, or by a fine not exceeding one thousand dollars, or by both such fine and imprisonment at the discretion of the Court."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "Every person who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with a quick child</em>, any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or means whatever, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such woman, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for such purpose, shall, upon conviction, be punished by fine not exceeding one thousand dollars, and by confinement to hard labor not less than one year, nor more than ten years."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 80" name="FRopinion1.80" href="#FNopinion1.80">80</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>13. New Jersey (1849):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"That if any person or persons, maliciously or without lawful justification, with intent to cause and procure the miscarriage <em>of a woman then pregnant with child</em>, shall administer to her, prescribe for her, or advise or direct her to take or swallow any poison, drug, medicine, or noxious thing; and if any person or persons maliciously, and without lawful justification, shall use any instrument or means whatever, with the like intent; and every person, with the like intent, knowingly aiding and assisting such offender or offenders, shall, on conviction thereof, be adjudged guilty of a high misdemeanor; and if the woman die in consequence thereof, shall be punished by fine, not exceeding one thousand dollars, or imprisonment at hard labour for any term not exceeding fifteen years, or both; and if the woman doth not die in consequence thereof, such offender shall, on conviction thereof, be adjudged guilty of a misdemeanor, and be punished by fine, not exceeding five hundred dollars, or imprisonment at hard labour, for any term not exceeding seven years, or both."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 81" name="FRopinion1.81" href="#FNopinion1.81">81</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>14. California (1850):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 45. "And every person who shall administer or cause to be administered or taken, any medical substances, or shall use or cause to be used any instruments whatever, with the intention <em>to procure the miscarriage of any woman then being with child</em>, and shall be thereof duly convicted, shall be punished by imprisonment in the State Prison for a term not less than two years, nor more than five years: Provided, that no physician shall be affected by the last clause of this section, who, in the discharge of his professional duties, deems it necessary to produce the miscarriage of any woman in order to save her life."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 82" name="FRopinion1.82" href="#FNopinion1.82">82</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>15. Texas (1854):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "If any person, with the intent to procure the miscarriage <em>of any woman being with child</em>, unlawfully and maliciously shall administer to her or cause to be taken by her any poison or other noxious thing, or shall use any instrument or any means whatever, with like intent, every such offender, and every person counselling or aiding or abetting such offender, shall be punished by confinement to hard labor in the Penitentiary not exceeding ten years."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 83" name="FRopinion1.83" href="#FNopinion1.83">83</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>16. Louisiana (1856):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 24. "Whoever shall feloniously administer or cause to be administered any drug, potion, or any other thing to any woman, for the purpose of procuring a premature delivery, and whoever shall administer or cause to be administered <em>to any woman pregnant with child</em>, any drug, potion, or any other thing, for the purpose of procuring abortion, or a premature delivery, shall be imprisoned at hard labor, for not less than one, nor more than ten years."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 84" name="FRopinion1.84" href="#FNopinion1.84">84</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>17. Iowa (1858):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "That every person who shall willfully administer <em>to</em> <em>any pregnant woman</em>, any medicine, drug, substance or thing whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means whatever, with the intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of any such woman, unless the same shall be necessary to preserve the life of such woman, shall upon conviction thereof, be punished by imprisonment in the county jail for a term of not exceeding one year, and be fined in a sum not exceeding one thousand dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 85" name="FRopinion1.85" href="#FNopinion1.85">85</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>18. Wisconsin (1858):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 11. "Every person who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with a child</em> any medicine, drug, or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such mother, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for such purpose, shall, in case the death of such child or of such mother be thereby produced, be deemed guilty of manslaughter in the second degree."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 86" name="FRopinion1.86" href="#FNopinion1.86">86</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 58. "Every person who shall administer <em>to any pregnant woman</em>, or prescribe for any such woman, or advise or procure any such woman to take, any medicine, drug, or substance or thing whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means whatever, or advise or procure the same to be used, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of any such woman, shall upon conviction be punished by imprisonment in a county jail, not more than one year nor less than three months, or by fine, not exceeding five hundred dollars, or by both fine and imprisonment, at the discretion of the court."</p>
</blockquote><p><strong>19. Kansas (1859):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 10. "Every person who shall administer <em>to any woman, pregnant with a quick child</em>, any medicine, drug or substance whatsoever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such mother, or shall have been advised by a physician to be necessary for that purpose, shall be deemed guilty of manslaughter in the second degree."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 37. "Every physician or other person who shall wilfully administer <em>to any pregnant woman</em> any medicine, drug or substance whatsoever, or shall use or employ any instrument or means whatsoever, with intent thereby to procure abortion or the miscarriage of any such woman, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such woman, or shall have been advised by a physician to be necessary for that purpose, shall, upon conviction, be adjudged guilty of a misdemeanor, and punished by imprisonment in a county jail not exceeding one year, or by fine not exceeding five hundred dollars, or by both such fine and imprisonment."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 87" name="FRopinion1.87" href="#FNopinion1.87">87</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>20. Connecticut (1860):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "That any person with intent <em>to procure the miscarriage or abortion of any woman</em>, shall give or administer to her, prescribe for her, or advise, or direct, or cause or procure her to take, any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or use or advise the use of any instrument, or other means whatever, with the like intent, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such woman, or of her unborn child, shall be deemed guilty of felony, and upon due conviction thereof shall be punished by imprisonment in the Connecticut state prison, not more than five years or less than one year, or by a fine of one thousand dollars, or both, at the discretion of the court."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 88" name="FRopinion1.88" href="#FNopinion1.88">88</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>21. Pennsylvania (1860):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 87. "If any person shall unlawfully administer <em>to any woman, pregnant or quick with child, or supposed and believed to be pregnant or quick with child</em>, any drug, poison, or other substance whatsoever, or shall unlawfully use any instrument or other means whatsoever, with the intent to procure the miscarriage of such woman, and such woman, or any child with which she may be quick, shall die in consequence of either of said unlawful acts, the person so offending shall be guilty of felony, and shall be sentenced to pay a fine not exceeding five hundred dollars, and to undergo an imprisonment, by separate or solitary confinement at labor, not exceeding seven years."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 88. "If any person, with intent <em>to procure the miscarriage of any woman</em>, shall unlawfully administer to her any poison, drug or substance whatsoever, or shall unlawfully use any instrument, or other means whatsoever, with the like intent, such person shall be guilty of felony, and being thereof convicted, shall be sentenced to pay a fine not exceeding five hundred dollars, and undergo an imprisonment, by separate or solitary confinement at labor, not exceeding three years."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 89" name="FRopinion1.89" href="#FNopinion1.89">89</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>22. Rhode Island (1861):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "Every person who shall be convicted of wilfully administering <em>to any pregnant woman, or to any woman supposed by such person to be pregnant</em>, anything whatever, or shall employ any means whatever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of such woman, unless the same is necessary to preserve her life, shall be imprisoned not exceeding one year, or fined not exceeding one thousand dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 90" name="FRopinion1.90" href="#FNopinion1.90">90</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>23. Nevada (1861):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 42. "[E]very person who shall administer, or cause to be administered or taken, any medicinal substance, or shall use, or cause to be used, any instruments whatever, with the intention <em>to procure the miscarriage of any woman then being with child</em>, and shall be thereof duly convicted, shall be punished by imprisonment in the Territorial prison, for a term not less than two years, nor more than five years; provided, that no physician shall be affected by the last clause of this section, who, in the discharge of his professional duties, deems it necessary to produce the miscarriage of any woman in order to save her life."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 91" name="FRopinion1.91" href="#FNopinion1.91">91</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>24. West Virginia (1863):</strong></p>
<p><em>West Virginia's Constitution adopted the laws of Virginia when it became its own State:</em></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"Such parts of the common law and of the laws of the State of Virginia as are in force within the boundaries of the State of West Virginia, when this Constitution goes into operation, and are not repugnant thereto, shall be and continue the law of this State until altered or repealed by the Legislature."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 92" name="FRopinion1.92" href="#FNopinion1.92">92</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><em>The Virginia law in force in 1863 stated</em>:</p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 8. "Any free person who shall administer to, or cause to be taken, <em>by a woman</em>, any drug or other thing, or use any means, with intent to destroy her unborn child, or to produce abortion or miscarriage, and shall thereby destroy such child, or produce such abortion or miscarriage, shall be confined in the penitentiary not less than one, nor more than five years.  No person, by reason of any act mentioned in this section, shall be punishable where such act is done in good faith, with the intention of saving the life of such woman or child."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 93" name="FRopinion1.93" href="#FNopinion1.93">93</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>25. Oregon (1864):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 509. "If any person shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with child</em>, any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall be necessary to preserve the life of such mother, such person shall, in case the death of such child or mother be thereby produced, be deemed guilty of manslaughter."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 94" name="FRopinion1.94" href="#FNopinion1.94">94</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>26. Nebraska (1866):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 42. "Every person who shall willfully and maliciously administer or cause to be administered to or taken by any person, any poison or other noxious or destructive substance or liquid, with the intention to cause the death of such person, and being thereof duly convicted, shall be punished by confinement in the penitentiary for a term not less than one year and not more than seven years.  And every person who shall administer or cause to be administered or taken, any such poison, substance or liquid, with the intention <em>to procure the miscarriage</em> <em>of any woman then being with child</em>, and shall thereof be duly convicted, shall be imprisoned for a term not exceeding three years in the penitentiary, and fined in a sum not exceeding one thousand dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 95" name="FRopinion1.95" href="#FNopinion1.95">95</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>27. Maryland (1868):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "And be it enacted, That any person who shall knowingly advertise, print, publish, distribute or circulate, or knowingly cause to be advertised, printed, published, distributed or circulated, any pamphlet, printed paper, book, newspaper notice, advertisement or reference containing words or language, giving or conveying any notice, hint or reference to any person, or to the name of any person real or fictitious, from whom; or to any place, house, shop or office, when any poison, drug, mixture, preparation, medicine or noxious thing, or any instrument or means whatever; for the purpose of producing abortion, or who shall knowingly sell, or cause to be sold any such poison, drug, mixture, preparation, medicine or noxious thing or instrument of any kind whatever; or where any advice, direction, information or knowledge may be obtained <em>for the purpose of causing the miscarriage or abortion of any woman pregnant with child, at any period of her pregnancy</em>, or shall knowingly sell or cause to be sold any medicine, or who shall knowingly use or cause to be used any means whatsoever for that purpose, shall be punished by imprisonment in the penitentiary for not less than three years, or by a fine of not less than five hundred nor more than one thousand dollars, or by both, in the discretion of the Court; and in case of fine being imposed, one half thereof shall be paid to the State of Maryland, and one-half to the School Fund of the city or county where the offence was committed; provided, however, that nothing herein contained shall be construed so as to prohibit the supervision and management by a regular practitioner of medicine of all cases of abortion occurring spontaneously, either as the result of accident, constitutional debility, or any other natural cause, or the production of abortion by a regular practitioner of medicine when, after consulting with one or more respectable physicians, he shall be satisfied that the foetus is dead, or that no other method will secure the safety of the mother."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 96" name="FRopinion1.96" href="#FNopinion1.96">96</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>28. Florida (1868):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ch. 3, Sec. 11. "Every person who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with a quick child</em> any medicine, drug, or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument, or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such mother, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for such purpose, shall, in case the death of such child or of such mother be thereby produced, be deemed guilty of manslaughter in the second degree."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ch. 8, Sec. 9. "Whoever, with intent <em>to procure miscarriage of any woman</em>, unlawfully administers to her, or advises, or prescribes for her, or causes to be taken by her, any poison, drug, medicine, or other noxious thing, or unlawfully uses any instrument or other means whatever with the like intent, or with like intent aids or assists therein, shall, if the woman does not die in consequence thereof, be punished by imprisonment in the State penittentiary not exceeding seven years, nor less than one year, or by fine not exceeding one thousand dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 97" name="FRopinion1.97" href="#FNopinion1.97">97</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>29. Minnesota (1873):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "That any person who shall administer <em>to any woman with child</em>, or prescribe for any such woman, or suggest to, or advise, or procure her to take any medicine, drug, substance or thing whatever, or who shall use or employ, or advise or suggest the use or employment of any instrument or other means or force whatever, with intent thereby to cause or procure the miscarriage or abortion or premature labor of any such woman, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve her life, or the life of such child, shall, in case the death of such child or of such woman results in whole or in part therefrom, be deemed guilty of a felony, and upon conviction thereof, shall be punished by imprisonment in the state prison for a term not more than ten (10) years nor less than three (3) years."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "Any person who shall administer <em>to any woman with child</em>, or prescribe, or procure, or provide for any such woman, or suggest to, or advise, or procure any such woman to take any medicine, drug, substance or thing whatever, or shall use or employ, or suggest, or advise the use or employment of any instrument or other means or force whatever, with intent thereby to cause or procure the miscarriage or abortion or premature labor of any such woman, shall upon conviction thereof be punished by imprisonment in the state prison for a term not more than two years nor less than one year, or by fine not more than five thousand dollars nor less than five hundred dollars, or by such fine and imprisonment both, at the discretion of the court."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 98" name="FRopinion1.98" href="#FNopinion1.98">98</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>30. Arkansas (1875):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "That it shall be unlawful for any one to administer or prescribe any medicine or drugs <em>to any woman with child</em>, with intent to produce an abortion, or premature delivery of any foetus before the period of quickening, or to produce or attempt to produce such abortion by any other means; and any person offending against the provision of this section, shall be fined in any sum not exceeding one thousand ($1000) dollars, and imprisoned in the penitentiary not less than one (1) nor more than five (5) years; provided, that this section shall not apply to any abortion produced by any regular practicing physician, for the purpose of saving the mother's life."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 99" name="FRopinion1.99" href="#FNopinion1.99">99</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>31. Georgia (1876):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "That every person who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with a child</em>, any medicine, drug, or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such mother, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for such purpose, shall, in case the death of such child or mother be thereby produced, be declared guilty of an assault with intent to murder."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 3. "That any person who shall wilfully administer <em>to any pregnant woman</em> any medicine, drug or substance, or anything whatever, or shall employ any instrument or means whatever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage or abortion of any such woman, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such woman, or shall have been advised by two physicians to be necessary for that purpose, shall, upon conviction, be punished as prescribed in section 4310 of the Revised Code of Georgia."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 100" name="FRopinion1.100" href="#FNopinion1.100">100</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>32. North Carolina (1881):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "That every person who shall wilfully administer <em>to any woman either pregnant or quick with child</em>, or prescribe for any such woman, or advise or procure any such woman to take any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means with intent thereby to destroy said child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of  such mother, shall be guilty of a felony, and shall be imprisoned in the state penitentiary for not less than one year nor more than ten years, and be fined at the discretion of the court."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "That every person who shall administer <em>to any pregnant woman</em>, or prescribe for any such woman, or advise and procure such woman to take any medicine, drug or any thing whatsoever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of any such woman, or to injure or destroy such woman, or shall use any instrument or application for any of the above purposes, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and, on conviction, shall be imprisoned in the jail or state penitentiary for not less than one year or more than five years, and fined at the discretion of the court."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 101" name="FRopinion1.101" href="#FNopinion1.101">101</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>33. Delaware (1883):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "Every person who, with the intent to procure the miscarriage <em>of any pregnant woman or women supposed by such person to be pregnant</em>, unless the same be necessary to preserve her life, shall administer to her, advise, or prescribe for her, or cause to be taken by her any poison, drug, medicine, or other noxious thing, or shall use any instrument or other means whatsoever, or shall aid, assist, or counsel any person so intending to procure a miscarriage, whether said miscarriage be accomplished or not, shall be guilty of a felony, and upon conviction thereof shall be fined not less than one hundred dollars nor more than five hundred dollars and be imprisoned for a term not exceeding five years nor less than one year."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 102" name="FRopinion1.102" href="#FNopinion1.102">102</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>34. Tennessee (1883):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "That every person who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with child, whether such child be quick or not</em>, any medicine, drug or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument, or other means whatever with intent to destroy such child, and shall thereby destroy such child before its birth, unless the same shall have been done with a view to preserve the life of the mother, shall be punished by imprisonment in the penitentiary not less than one nor more than five years."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "Every person who shall administer any substance with the intention <em>to procure the miscarriage</em> <em>of a woman then being with child</em>, or shall use or employ any instrument or other means with such intent, unless the same shall have been done with a view to preserve the life of such mother, shall be punished by imprisonment in the penitentiary not less than one nor more than three years."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 103" name="FRopinion1.103" href="#FNopinion1.103">103</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>35. South Carolina (1883):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "That any person who shall administer <em>to any woman with child</em>, or prescribe for any such woman, or suggest to or advise or procure her to take, any medicine, substance, drug or thing whatever, or who shall use or employ, or advise the use or employment of, any instrument or other means of force whatever, with intent thereby to cause or procure the miscarriage or abortion or premature labor of any such woman, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve her life, or the life of such child, shall, in case the death of such child or of such woman results in whole or in part therefrom, be deemed guilty of a felony, and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished by imprisonment in the Penitentiary for a term not more than twenty years nor less than five years."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "That any person who shall administer <em>to any woman with child</em>, or prescribe or procure or provide for any such woman, or advise or procure any such woman to take, any medicine, drug, substance or thing whatever, or shall use or employ or advise the use or employment of, any instrument or other means of force whatever, with intent thereby to cause or procure the miscarriage or abortion or premature labor of any such woman, shall, upon conviction thereof, be punished by imprisonment in the Penitentiary for a term not more than five years, or by fine not more than five thousand dollars, or by such fine and imprisonment both, at the discretion of the Court; but no conviction shall be had under the provisions of Section 1 or 2 of this Act upon the uncorroborated evidence of such woman."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 104" name="FRopinion1.104" href="#FNopinion1.104">104</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>36. Kentucky (1910):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "It shall be unlawful for any person to prescribe or administer <em>to any pregnant woman, or to any woman whom he has reason to believe pregnant, at any time during the period of gestation</em>, any drug, medicine or substance, whatsoever, with the intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of such woman, or with like intent, to use any instrument or means whatsoever, unless such miscarriage is necessary to preserve her life; and any person so offending, shall be punished by a fine of not less than five hundred nor more than one thousand dollars, and imprisoned in the State prison for not less than one nor more than ten years."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "If by reason of any of the acts described in Section 1 hereof, the miscarriage of such woman is procured, and she does miscarry, causing the death of the unborn child, whether before or after quickening time, the person so offending shall be guilty of a felony, and confined in the penitentiary for not less than two, nor more than twenty-one years."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 3. "If, by reason of the commission of any of the acts described in Section 1 hereof, the woman to whom such drug or substance has been administered, or upon whom such instrument has been used, shall die, the person offending shall be punished as now prescribed by law, for the offense of murder or manslaughter, as the facts may justify."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 4. "The consent of the woman to the performance of the operation or administering of the medicines or substances, referred to, shall be no defense, and she shall be a competent witness in any prosecution under this act, and for that purpose she shall not be considered an accomplice."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 105" name="FRopinion1.105" href="#FNopinion1.105">105</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>37. Mississippi (1952):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "Whoever, by means of any instrument, medicine, drug, or other means whatever shall willfully and knowingly cause <em>any woman pregnant with child</em> to abort or miscarry, or attempts to procure or produce an abortion or miscarriage, unless the same were done as necessary for the preservation of the mother's life, shall be imprisoned in the state penitentiary no less than one (1) year, nor more than ten (10) years; or if the death of the mother results therefrom, the person procuring, causing, or attempting to procure or cause the abortion or miscarriage shall be guilty of murder."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "No act prohibited in section 1 hereof shall be considered as necessary for the preservation of the mother's life unless upon the prior advice, in writing, of two reputable licensed physicians."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 3. "The license of any physician or nurse shall be automatically revoked upon conviction under the provisions of this act."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 106" name="FRopinion1.106" href="#FNopinion1.106">106</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><h2><p align="CENTER">B</p>
</h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This appendix contains statutes criminalizing abortion at all stages in each of the Territories that became States and in the District of Columbia.  The statutes appear in chronological order of enactment.</p>
<p><strong>1. Hawaii (1850):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "Whoever maliciously, without lawful justification, administers, or causes or procures to be administered any poison or noxious thing <em>to a woman then with child</em>, in order to produce her mis-carriage, or maliciously uses any instrument or other means with like intent, shall, if such woman be then quick with child, be punished by fine not exceeding one thousand dollars and imprisonment at hard labor not more than five years.  And if she be then not quick with child, shall be punished by a fine not exceeding five hundred dollars, and imprisonment at hard labor not more than two years."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "Where means of causing abortion are used for the purpose of saving the life of the woman, the surgeon or other person using such means is lawfully justified."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 107" name="FRopinion1.107" href="#FNopinion1.107">107</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>2. Washington (1854):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 37. "Every person who shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with a quick child</em>, any medicine, drug, or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument, or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall have been necessary to preserve the life of such mother, shall, in case the death of such child or of such mother be thereby produced, on conviction thereof, be imprisoned in the penitentiary not more than twenty years, nor less than one year."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 38. "Every person who shall administer <em>to any pregnant woman, or to any woman who he supposes to be pregnant</em>, any medicine, drug, or substance whatever, or shall use or employ any instrument, or other means, thereby to procure the miscarriage of such woman, unless the same is necessary to preserve her life, shall on conviction thereof, be imprisoned in the penitentiary not more than five years, nor less than one year, or be imprisoned in the county jail not more than twelve months, nor less than one month, and be fined in any sum not exceeding one thousand dollars."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 108" name="FRopinion1.108" href="#FNopinion1.108">108</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>3. Colorado (1861):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 42.  "[E]very person who shall administer substance or liquid, or who shall use or cause to be used any instrument, of whatsoever kind, with the intention <em>to procure the miscarriage of any woman then being with child</em>, and shall thereof be duly convicted, shall be imprisoned for a term not exceeding three years, and fined in a sum not exceeding one thousand dollars; and if any woman, by reason of such treatment, shall die, the person or persons administering, or causing to be administered, such poison, substance or liquid, or using or causing to be used, any instrument, as aforesaid, shall be deemed guilty of manslaughter, and if convicted, be punished accordingly."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 109" name="FRopinion1.109" href="#FNopinion1.109">109</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>4. Idaho (1864):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 42. "[E]very person who shall administer or cause to be administered, or taken, any medicinal substance, or shall use or cause to be used, any instruments whatever, with the intention <em>to procure the miscarriage of any woman then being with child</em>, and shall be thereof duly convicted, shall be punished by imprisonment in the territorial prison for a term not less than two years, nor more than five years: <em>Provided</em>, That no physician shall be effected by the last clause of this section, who in the discharge of his professional duties, deems it necessary to produce the miscarriage of any woman in order to save her life."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 110" name="FRopinion1.110" href="#FNopinion1.110">110</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>5. Montana (1864):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 41. "[E]very person who shall administer, or cause to be administered, or taken, any medicinal substance, or shall use, or cause to be used, any instruments whatever, with the intention <em>to produce the miscarriage of any woman then being with child</em>, and shall be thereof duly convicted, shall be punished by imprisonment in the Territorial prison for a term not less than two years nor more than five years.  <em>Provided</em>, That no physician shall be affected by the last clause of this section, who in the discharge of his professional duties deems it necessary to produce the miscarriage of any woman in order to save her life."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 111" name="FRopinion1.111" href="#FNopinion1.111">111</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>6. Arizona (1865):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 45. "[E]very person who shall administer or cause to be administered or taken, any medicinal substances, or shall use or cause to be used any instruments whatever, with the intention <em>to procure the miscarriage of any woman then being with child</em>, and shall be thereof duly convicted, shall be punished by imprisonment in the Territorial prison for a term not less than two years nor more than five years: Provided, that no physician shall be affected by the last clause of this section, who in the discharge of his professional duties, deems it necessary to produce the miscarriage of any woman in order to save her life."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 112" name="FRopinion1.112" href="#FNopinion1.112">112</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>7. Wyoming (1869):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 25. "[A]ny person who shall administer, or cause to be administered, or taken, any such poison, substance or liquid, or who shall use, or cause to be used, any instrument of whatsoever kind, with the intention <em>to procure the miscarriage of any woman then being with child</em>, and shall thereof be duly convicted, shall be imprisoned for a term not exceeding three years, in the penitentiary, and fined in a sum not exceeding one thousand dollars; and if any woman by reason of such treatment shall die, the person, or persons, administering, or causing to be administered such poison, substance, or liquid, or using or causing to be used, any instrument, as aforesaid, shall be deemed guilty of manslaughter, and if convicted, be punished by imprisonment for a term not less than three years in the penitentiary, and fined in a sum not exceeding one thousand dollars, unless it appear that such miscarriage was procured or attempted by, or under advice of a physician or surgeon, with intent to save the life of such woman, or to prevent serious and permanent bodily injury to her."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 113" name="FRopinion1.113" href="#FNopinion1.113">113</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>8. Utah (1876):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 142. "Every person who provides, supplies, or administers <em>to any pregnant woman</em>, or procures any such woman to take any medicine, drug, or substance, or uses or employs any instrument or other means whatever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of such woman, unless the same is necessary to preserve her life, is punishable by imprisonment in the penitentiary not less than two nor more than ten years."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 114" name="FRopinion1.114" href="#FNopinion1.114">114</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>9. North Dakota (1877):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 337. "Every person who administers <em>to any pregnant woman</em>, or who prescribes for any such woman, or advises or procures any such woman to take any medicine, drug or substance, or uses or employs any instrument, or other means whatever with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of such woman, unless the same is necessary to preserve her life, is punishable by imprisonment in the territorial prison not exceeding three years, or in a county jail not exceeding one year."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 115" name="FRopinion1.115" href="#FNopinion1.115">115</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>10. South Dakota (1877):</strong> <em>Same as North Dakota</em>.</p>
<p><strong>11. Oklahoma (1890):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2187. "Every person who administers <em>to any pregnant woman</em>, or who prescribes for any such woman, or advises or procures any such woman to take any medicine, drug or substance, or uses or employs any instrument, or other means whatever, with intent thereby to procure the miscarriage of such woman, unless the same is necessary to preserve her life, is punishable by imprisonment in the Territorial prison not exceeding three years, or in a county jail not exceeding one year."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 116" name="FRopinion1.116" href="#FNopinion1.116">116</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>12. Alaska (1899):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 8. "That if any person shall administer <em>to any woman pregnant with a child</em> any medicine, drug, or substance whatever, or shall use any instrument or other means, with intent thereby to destroy such child, unless the same shall be necessary to preserve the life of such mother, such person shall, in case the death of such child or mother be thereby produced, be deemed guilty of manslaughter, and shall be punished accordingly."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 117" name="FRopinion1.117" href="#FNopinion1.117">117</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p><strong>13. New Mexico (1919):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 1. "Any person who shall administer <em>to any pregnant woman any medicine</em>, drug or substance whatever, or attempt by operation or any other method or means to produce an abortion or miscarriage upon such woman, shall be guilty of a felony, and, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined not more than two thousand ($2,000.00) Dollars, nor less than five hundred ($500.00) Dollars, or imprisoned in the penitentiary for a period of not less than one nor more than five years, or by both such fine and imprisonment in the discretion of the court trying the case."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 2. "Any person committing such act or acts mentioned in section one hereof which shall culminate in the death of the woman shall be deemed guilty of murder in the second degree; <em>Provided</em>, however, an abortion may be produced when two physicians licensed to practice in the State of New Mexico, in consultation, deem it necessary to preserve the life of the woman, or to prevent serious and permanent bodily injury."</p>
</blockquote><blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 3. "For the purpose of the act, the term "pregnancy" is defined as that condition of a woman <em>from the date of conception to the birth of her child</em>."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 118" name="FRopinion1.118" href="#FNopinion1.118">118</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><h2><p align="CENTER">*  *  *</p>
</h2><p><strong>District of Columbia (1901):</strong></p>
<blockquote><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sec. 809. "Whoever, with intent <em>to procure the miscarriage</em> <em>of any woman</em>, prescribes or administers to her any medicine, drug, or substance whatever, or with like intent uses any instrument or means, unless when necessary to preserve her life or health and under the direction of a competent licensed practitioner of medicine, shall be imprisoned for not more than five years; or if the woman or her child dies in consequence of such act, by imprisonment for not less than three nor more than twenty years."<sup><a aria-label="Move to footnote 119" name="FRopinion1.119" href="#FNopinion1.119">119</a></sup></p>
</blockquote><p></p><hr>





<p align="CENTER"><span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Thomas, J.</small></span>, concurring</p>
<p align="CENTER"> 597 U.&nbsp;S. ____ (2022)</p>


<p align="CENTER">No. 19-1392</p>


<center><h2><p align="CENTER">THOMAS E. DOBBS, STATE HEALTH OFFICER OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH, <span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>et&nbsp;al</small></span>., PETITIONERS <em>v.</em> JACKSON WOMEN'S HEALTH ORGANIZATION, <span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>et&nbsp;al.</small></span></p>
</h2></center><center><h4><p align="CENTER"><span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>on writ of certiorari to the united states court of appeals for the fifth circuit</small></span></p>
</h4></center><center><p align="CENTER">[June 24, 2022]</p>
</center><p></p><hr>

<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Justice Thomas</small></span>, concurring.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I join the opinion of the Court because it correctly holds that there is no constitutional right to abortion.  Respondents invoke one source for that right: the Fourteenth Amendment's guarantee that no State shall "deprive any person of life, liberty, or property without due process of law."  The Court well explains why, under our substantive due process precedents, the purported right to abortion is not a form of "liberty" protected by the Due Process Clause.  Such a right is neither "deeply rooted in this Nation's history and tradition" nor "implicit in the concept of ordered liberty."  <em>Washington</em> v. <em>Glucksberg</em>, 521 U.&nbsp;S. 702, 721 (1997) (internal quotation marks omitted).  "[T]he idea that the Framers of the Fourteenth Amendment understood the Due Process Clause to protect a right to abortion is farcical."  <em>June Medical Services L.&nbsp;L.</em>&nbsp;<em>C.</em> v. <em>Russo</em>, 591 U.&nbsp;S. ___, ___ (2020) (<span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Thomas</small></span>, J., dissenting) (slip op., at 17).</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I write separately to emphasize a second, more fundamental reason why there is no abortion guarantee lurking in the Due Process Clause.  Considerable historical evidence indicates that "due process of law" merely required executive and judicial actors to comply with legislative enactments and the common law when depriving a person of life, liberty, or property.  See, <em>e.g.,</em> <em>Johnson</em> v. <em>United States</em>, 576 U.&nbsp;S. 591, 623 (2015) (<span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Thomas</small></span>, J., concurring in judgment).  Other sources, by contrast, suggest that "due process of law" prohibited legislatures "from authorizing the deprivation of a person's life, liberty, or property without providing him the customary procedures to which freemen were entitled by the old law of England."  <em>United States</em> v. <em>Vaello Madero</em>, 596 U.&nbsp;S. ___, ____ (2022) (<span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Thomas</small></span>, J., concurring) (slip op., at 3) (internal quotation marks omitted).  Either way, the Due Process Clause at most guarantees <em>process</em>.
